# walkthrough.md

Schema: `v1`
Last updated: `2026-04-09`

## Project Snapshot
- long-term objective: compare integrated navigation algorithm combinations and study observability under different sensor schedules and constraints
- current baseline config: `config_data2_baseline_ins_gnss_outage_best.yaml`; `config_data5_baseline_ins_gnss_outage_best.yaml`
- state dimension and active filter modes: `kStateDim = 31`; standard `ESKF` and unified `InEKF` switch via `fusion.inekf.enable`

## Open Hypotheses
| hyp_id | hypothesis | evidence so far | next check | status |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| `HYP-1` | Re-running `data5_baseline_ins_gnss_outage_kf_gins_contract_r1` on the current solver will reproduce the original metrics within negligible numerical drift and should not materially change phase3 outage accuracy | `2026-04-06` exact-case-config fresh rerun into `output/data5_baseline_ins_gnss_outage_kf_gins_contract_r2_casecfg/` instead produced catastrophic divergence: `overall_rmse3d=9.988212940e9 m`, `overall_final_3d=3.464821173e10 m`, and `BuildProcessModel` emitted repeated `h out of range` / `v_ned too large` warnings near the tail | audit solver/code changes between `build/Release/eskf_fusion.exe @ 2026-03-29 20:32:55 local` reference era and current `2026-04-06 13:26:23 local` build; identify when data5 outage contract regressed | `rejected` |
| `HYP-2` | The canonical standard-ESKF IMU error-state contract in this solver is: keep `F_v,ba/F_v,sa` negative under `δb = b_true - b_hat`, keep IMU nominal error injection additive (`state_.ba/bg/sg/sa += d*`), and use positive `F_φ,bg/F_φ,sg` under the solver's `q_true ≈ q_hat ⊗ Exp(-φ_e)` attitude-error convention | fresh regression helpers now cover IMU error injection consistency, standard-ESKF error-state round-trip, and finite-difference process-model coupling; `build\\Release\\regression_checks.exe` passes only with `state_.bg += dbg`, `F_v,ba/F_v,sa < 0`, and `F_φ,bg/F_φ,sg > 0`. The same contract recovers `EXP-20260406-data5-kf-sparse15s-compare-r3` to `rmse3d=0.068141 m` from `r2`'s `6.057096 m` | rerun the remaining official data2/data5 acceptance cases under this audited contract and retire the provisional `restore_check_r3` interpretation | `validated` |
| `HYP-3` | The current data2 GNSS correction weakness is caused by GNSS updates being applied at generic IMU sample times rather than at `t_gnss` | code audit of `src/app/pipeline_fusion.cpp` showed `PredictCurrentIntervalWithExactGnss()` splits IMU intervals and calls `RunGnssUpdate()` at `mid_imu.t == t_gnss`; offline replay on the exact data2 baseline window produced `split=2412`, `align_prev=0`, `align_curr=0`, `stale=0` after truth-anchor cropping | test the remaining timing risk: whether `dataset/data2_converted/IMU_converted.txt` timestamps are interval-end, midpoint, or interval-start semantics | `rejected` |
| `HYP-4` | Even though the current pipeline updates at `t_gnss`, a hidden IMU timestamp-semantics mismatch (end vs midpoint/start) could still bias the split propagation and weaken GNSS correction | `BuildImuSequence()` interprets row `i` as increment over `(t_{i-1}, t_i]`; this assumption is not validated by the binary converter, which only copies raw timestamps and increments. The first post-crop GNSS samples fall near the start of the code-assumed IMU interval (for example `528077.0` lies `0.630 ms` after `imu_prev=528076.999370` and `4.371 ms` before `imu_curr=528077.004371`) | run a minimal A/B experiment with timestamp reinterpretation or equivalent `±0.5dt` time shifts and compare pre-outage INS/GNSS behavior / first GNSS residual | `open` |
| `HYP-5` | The data5 full-window sparse-15s regression was caused by an inconsistent standard-ESKF IMU sign convention in the shared INS/GNSS path, not by the sparse-GNSS contract itself | under the unchanged sparse-15s contract, `EXP-20260406-data5-kf-sparse15s-compare-r2` had current `rmse3d=6.057096 m` vs KF-GINS `0.054833 m`; after restoring the audited sign contract, `EXP-20260406-data5-kf-sparse15s-compare-r3` recovered current to `rmse3d=0.068141 m`, `final_3d=0.018918 m`, with `bg/sg` trajectories now largely co-directional with `KF-GINS` and residual shared-state deltas reduced to tens of ppm / single-digit mGal | replay the same audited contract on the remaining outage acceptance cases and confirm whether any residual discrepancy survives outside the sparse-15s forensic window | `validated` |
| `HYP-6` | State semantics and filter conventions can be extracted into a dedicated contract layer without breaking legacy include consumers in Task 1 | red/green Task 1 checks passed; convergence `r2` moved `BuildFilterSemanticsFromLegacyFej(...)` into `navigation/filter_contracts.*`, added explicit branch tests (`disabled→standard`, `enabled+false→hybrid`, `enabled+true→true`), and expanded catalog assertions to full default block set including `odo_scale`, `mounting_roll/pitch/yaw`, `lever`, `gnss_lever`; fresh `build\\Release\\regression_checks.exe` remained `PASS` | use these contract tests as non-regression gate while Task 2 migrates internals | `validated` |
| `HYP-7` | The large `data2` `true_iekf` `GNSS_POS:att` Jacobian mismatch now seen in `output/_tmp_jacobian_refactor_check/` predates the Task 3 typed-input/context refactor rather than being introduced by it | this hypothesis is superseded by the direct fix-and-rerun result: after changing `src/navigation/measurement_model_gnss.cpp` so the true-InEKF attitude Jacobian linearizes the body displacement `d_body`, the fresh Jacobian audit in `output/review/20260307-update-reset-consistency-r1/summary.md` reports `GNSS_POS pos/att/gnss_lever rel_fro=0.000000` on both `data2` and `data4` | none; the focused audit has already closed the block-level mismatch | `resolved_by_focused_audit_20260407-1830` |

| `HYP-15` | The near-overlap seen in `EXP-20260407-data2-ins-gnss-sparse10s-eskf-vs-inekf-r2` is not because the GNSS update chain silently falls back to `ESKF`; instead, the `InEKF` update is materially different at the residual / Jacobian / gain level, while the final corrected nominal state remains close under this pure `INS/GNSS` sparse-10s contract | direct `gnss_updates` comparison over all `241` updates shows the chains are not bit-identical: `used_inekf=1` on the `InEKF` side; residual component deltas reach `|Δy_x|=0.3190 m`, `|Δy_y|=0.3230 m`; attitude Jacobian row deltas reach `||ΔH_att,x||_F=2.5465`, `||ΔH_att,y||_F=2.5472`; lever Jacobian row deltas reach `||ΔH_lever,x||_F=2.0000`; Kalman-gain row deltas reach `||ΔK_att,z||_F=0.04862`; innovation covariance deltas reach `||ΔS||_F=3.2924`. Yet the post-update corrected states remain very close: max `|Δp_after|=[0.000752, 0.000883, 0.001719] m`, max `|Δv_after|=[0.000118, 0.000214, 0.000321] m`, and earlier full-run state metrics still stay near-identical. The 2026-04-07 bug-doc audit additionally confirmed that `filter_reset.cpp` and `measurement_model_gnss.cpp` did contain real dead/redundant InEKF branches, but it rejected the stronger process-noise suspicion because `BuildContinuousNoiseCovariance()` already switches non-standard semantics to body-frame `G_vel/G_att` | trace one or two representative GNSS updates numerically through `measurement_model_gnss.cpp -> filter_engine.cpp -> filter_reset.cpp` after the dead-branch cleanup to decide whether the remaining near-overlap is expected basis-change dominance under this experiment or evidence that the process-side distinction is still too weak | `open` |
| `HYP-16` | On the pure `INS/GNSS` `data2` `60 s on / 100 s off` outage contract, replaying the canonical `ESKF best` noise baseline under unified `InEKF` should keep user-facing outage metrics nearly identical to the `ESKF best_r2` reference, with any difference staying at the mm-level rather than producing a new large performance separation | even after correcting the repo-level baseline semantic bug (`use_truth_pva=true -> false`) and forcing both fresh runs into `[Init] Mode: Manual`, `EXP-20260407-data2-baseline-ins-gnss-inekf-outage-60on100off-from-eskf-best-r1` still returns `overall_rmse3d=0.941943 m`, `phase3_rmse3d=1.117934 m`, `phase3_final_3d=1.387864 m`; versus corrected-baseline `EXP-20260407-data2-baseline-ins-gnss-eskf-outage-60on100off-best-r2`, deltas remain only `overall_rmse3d=-0.000705633 m`, `p95_3d=-0.001232600 m`, `phase3_rmse3d=-0.000837511 m`, while `phase3_final_3d=+0.001629791 m` and yaw/bg_z peaks stay effectively unchanged in user-facing terms | use this corrected-baseline outage replay pair as the canonical `ESKF/InEKF` reference under manual-init semantics; only reopen if harsher outage/init perturbations or later code changes move the deltas beyond numerical-near-equivalence | `validated` |
| `HYP-17` | The current unified `InEKF` runtime is genuinely applying a non-identity reset gamma on live pure `INS/GNSS` corrections; the near-overlap with `ESKF` is therefore not explained by `Gamma` collapsing to `I` globally | fresh `build/Release/regression_checks.exe` prints `[DIAG] Gamma deviation from I: 0.0110205` and `[DIAG] dx_att norm: 0.001077` on the dedicated InEKF reset parity case. The corrected-baseline manual-init outage replay `EXP-20260407-data2-baseline-ins-gnss-inekf-outage-60on100off-from-eskf-best-r1` still records `1359` reset diagnostics with `gamma_min=0.0004591`, `gamma_p50=0.00695686`, `gamma_mean=0.03836948`, `gamma_p95=0.0211879`, `gamma_max=6.45095`; `1346/1359` are `>1e-3`, `344/1359` are `>1e-2`, `10/1359` are `>1`, and `0/1359` are `<1e-4`. Meanwhile `dx_att` stays small but nonzero (`dx_p50=1.04447e-05`, `dx_mean=2.817806e-05`, `dx_max=0.0011978`) | when tracing representative sparse-10s GNSS updates, decompose which `rho_p_body/rho_v_body/phi_body` terms dominate the few large `gamma_diff > 1` spikes and whether they align with specific GNSS residual bursts | `validated` |
| `HYP-18` | The repo-level baseline semantic bug `fusion.init.use_truth_pva=true` is real and must be fixed, but disabling it alone will not materially enlarge the current `data2` pure `INS/GNSS` outage-side `ESKF/InEKF` gap because the stored manual initial state is already nearly equal to the truth start | fresh config audit found multiple baseline/research-seed YAMLs incorrectly set `use_truth_pva: true`; after flipping them to `false`, fresh ESKF/InEKF outage reruns switch to `[Init] Mode: Manual` as intended. Yet the manual start position printed by both fresh runs is only `5.77e-05 m` away from the truth start position (`Δxyz=[-6.0e-06, -3.30e-05, 4.70e-05] m`), which explains why removing truth-init semantics does not materially move the outage metrics by itself | if the expectation is that outage should separate the filters more strongly, probe conditions that are not already near-truth at initialization: manual init perturbation, poorer attitude/bias priors, longer outages, or lever uncertainty | `validated` |
| `HYP-19` | Extending the GNSS-off duration from `100 s` to `150 s` in the current pure `INS/GNSS` manual-init contract will materially worsen outage accuracy for both filters, but by itself still will not produce a large `ESKF/InEKF` separation | fresh `60/150` replays raise the difficulty substantially: `ESKF phase3_rmse3d=2.715790 m` and `InEKF phase3_rmse3d=2.717070 m`, which are `+1.597019 m` and `+1.599136 m` worse than the corrected `60/100` references. Yet the longer-outage cross-filter gap remains tiny: `phase3_rmse3d delta=+0.001280081 m`, `overall_rmse3d delta=+0.001078529 m`, and `phase3_final_3d delta=-0.000005365 m` | if the goal is to force a visibly larger separation, combine longer outages with a stronger nonlinearity source such as perturbed manual init, larger lever uncertainty, or more aggressive prior/noise changes rather than relying on outage length alone | `validated` |
| `HYP-20` | Under the pure `INS/GNSS` `60/150` outage contract, injecting a large yaw-only manual-init error (`+10/+20/+30 deg`) will not create a dramatic `ESKF/InEKF` difference in initial yaw settle time, but it will expose a meaningful downstream robustness advantage for `InEKF` at larger offsets | fresh `EXP-20260407-data2-ins-gnss-outage-60on150off-yaw-init-compare-r1` shows stable-yaw settle times are either identical or only `1 s` faster on `InEKF`: at `+20 deg`, `settle_5deg` is `11.995 s` vs `12.995 s`; at `+30 deg`, `settle_2deg` is `13.995 s` vs `14.995 s`. However the later aggregate accuracy separates materially as the perturbation grows: `overall_rmse3d` is worse on `ESKF` by `0.058207 m` at `+20 deg` and by `0.319549 m` at `+30 deg`, while final 3D error remains mm-level close for both | inspect whether the robustness gap is already visible mainly in phase3 outage windows or whether it is seeded earlier during phase1/2 transient recovery; if needed, add a phase-wise summary to isolate where the larger-offset advantage appears | `validated` |
| `HYP-21` | Under the current `data2` staged `INS/GNSS/ODO/NHC` schedule, phase1 can identify the GNSS lever arm, but the phase2/phase3 `ODO/NHC` calibration states (`odo_scale`, `mounting_pitch/yaw`, `odo_lever`) remain only partially observable even when phase2 uses the intended covariance-only reset and the runtime mask-order bug is fixed | the earlier “no phase2 jump” symptom was real, but the root cause was runtime mask ordering rather than plotting: phase-entry `OverrideStateAndCov(...)` was executed while the old phase1 frozen mask was still active, so the freshly reset covariance for blocks `21-27` was immediately zeroed. After the 2026-04-08 15:58 fix, `DIAG_data2_ins_gnss_odo_nhc_staged_estimation_eskf.txt` shows the intended jump at `t=200.005537 s`: `std_odo_s=0.106743`, `std_mp=0.102286`, `std_my=0.102285`, `std_lx/std_ly/std_lz≈1.0 m`, whereas `t=198.005533 s` and `t=199.005536 s` were still zero. The 2026-04-08 16:53 rerun then switched the staged semantics to covariance-only phase2 reset and `60 s on / 60 s off` GNSS outage: the case config no longer contains `phase_entry_init_overrides`, but the same phase2 std jump still appears in `DIAG`. Under this fresh baseline, phase2 calibration behavior is unchanged at the block level (`odo_lever_y_err rmse=0.532570 m`; `mounting_pitch_err rmse=0.093659 deg`; `mounting_yaw_err rmse=0.550945 deg`; `odo_scale_err rmse=0.009071`), while the easier `60/60` outage improves navigation-side phase3 metrics (`phase3_rmse3d=0.246024 m`, `final_3d=0.039099 m`) without materially changing the residual calibration-state limits (`odo_lever_y_err rmse=0.119015 m`; `mounting_pitch_err rmse=0.102952 deg`; `mounting_yaw_err rmse=0.530575 deg`). The new 2026-04-08 joint300 merge test further strengthens the same conclusion: after collapsing the old phase1/phase2 split into a single `300 s` `INS/GNSS/ODO/NHC` estimation window and then freezing only `gnss_lever` under `60/100` outage, navigation and `odo_lever` behavior do not improve (`overall_rmse3d=0.491373 m`; post-300 `rmse3d=0.524804 m`; `odo_lever_y_err rmse phase1/phase2=0.856719/0.502781 m`), while `mounting_pitch/yaw` remain near their previous partially-observable plateau (`0.109716/0.536710 deg`) and `bg_z_err` still stays near `100 deg/h`. The latest full-run truth-fix controls split the two suspects directly. Fixing `odo_lever` to truth from phase1 yields only a modest navigation improvement (`overall_rmse3d 0.362315 -> 0.331770 m`, `phase3_rmse3d 0.429104 -> 0.392767 m`) while leaving `mounting_pitch/yaw` nearly unchanged (`phase3 rmse=0.101989/0.535306 deg`). Fixing `mounting` to truth from phase1 does not materially recover `odo_lever` (`phase2/3 odo_lever_y_err rmse=0.530695/0.119128 m`, almost unchanged from baseline) and instead degrades phase3 navigation severely (`phase3_rmse3d=1.975874 m`, `overall_rmse3d=1.664944 m`) with larger yaw/bg_z excursions. The new 3x3 odo-lever noise sweep adds one more constraint on the hypothesis: scalar odo-lever process-noise changes over `1e-6..1e-4` are numerically neutral, while phase2 `odo_lever` initial std is the only knob that moves the result materially. The current baseline `std=1.0 m` remains the best navigation point; `std=3.0 m` only improves `odo_lever_y` modestly (`phase3 rmse 0.118940 -> 0.112268 m`) at a slight navigation cost, and shrinking to `std=0.2 m` is clearly harmful (`phase3_rmse3d=0.434668 m`; `phase3 odo_lever_y_err rmse=0.263878 m`). The new 3x3 `bg_z` sweep closes off another simple explanation: neither loosening phase2 `bg_z` covariance to `10/30 deg/h` nor scaling z-axis gyro-bias process noise by `0.1x/1x/10x` recovers the mainline metrics. All scanned cases are worse than the preserved baseline, and even the least-bad case (`phase2_bgz_std=1 deg/h`, `q_z=0.1x`) still shifts `phase3_rmse3d 0.429104 -> 0.433283 m` while leaving `phase3 bg_z rmse` essentially unchanged (`100.032970 -> 100.028165 deg/h`). This means neither “merge the phases”, nor “treat mounting as the sole culprit”, nor “simple `bg_z` noise retuning” explains the main limitation. Even within the bias block, the dominant issue does not look like the tested scalar/z-axis `Q` or a looser phase2 `P0`, but rather the deeper coupled observability/excitation structure tying `bg_z` and blocks `21-27` together | keep both the baseline odo-lever settings and the baseline `bg_z` noise settings for the mainline staged contract. The next sweep should move away from simple noise retuning and toward structural interventions: phase2 excitation/window-length changes, `bg_z` observability-gate style mechanisms, or more targeted axis/block constraints that can change the coupling itself rather than just its prior/Q magnitudes | `open` |

- observability_notes: not a dedicated ablation. PVA errors stayed at centimeter-to-decimeter scale under the same sparse schedule, indicating the correction weakness was not due to GNSS weighting alone.
- decision: do not blindly copy `KF-GINS` signs into the current solver. Because the current solver uses additive IMU error injection with residuals formed as `y = z - h`, the evidence-backed standard-ESKF contract is `F_v,ba/F_v,sa < 0`, `state_.ba/bg/sg/sa += d*`, and `F_φ,bg/F_φ,sg > 0`. With that contract, the `data5` sparse-15s current solver recovers from the broken `r2` (`6.057096 m`) to `0.068141 m`, close to the historical `r1` scale and the `KF-GINS` reference.
- next_step: rerun the remaining official data2/data5 outage acceptance cases under the audited sign contract, then only if residual mismatches remain, revisit the narrower IMU timestamp-semantics hypothesis.

### session_id: 20260407-1459-data5_truth_loader_acceptance_recovery

5. ### session_id: 20260407-2020-inekf_core_contract_audit
- objective: answer whether the current unified `InEKF` implementation is mathematically on the intended core contract, specifically whether the `P/V/A` error is treated as a multiplicative body-frame invariant error rather than the old additive earth-frame error.
- scope: re-read `walkthrough.md`; audited the active unified `InEKF` semantic bridge, correction/reset path, process model, and measurement builders; traced the current pure `INS/GNSS` chain through `filter_contracts`, `filter_engine`, `filter_reset`, `process_model_inekf`, `measurement_model_gnss`, `measurement_model_common`, `measurement_model_road`, and `measurement_model_uwb`; distinguished the core `INS/GNSS` path from the broader 31-state integrated-navigation path; then recorded the code-level conclusion and remaining caveats here.
- changed_files: `walkthrough.md`
- configs: audit_scope=`unified InEKF code path only`; source_files=`include/navigation/state_defs.h`, `include/navigation/filter_contracts.h`, `src/navigation/filter_contracts.cpp`, `src/navigation/filter_engine.cpp`, `src/navigation/filter_reset.cpp`, `src/navigation/process_model_inekf.cpp`, `src/navigation/measurement_model_common.cpp`, `src/navigation/measurement_model_gnss.cpp`, `src/navigation/measurement_model_road.cpp`, `src/navigation/measurement_model_uwb.cpp`
- commands: `Get-Content walkthrough.md -TotalCount 140`; `rg -n "InEKF|RightInvariant|Invariant|body-frame|Body|Inject|error-state|phi" include\\navigation src\\navigation include\\core src\\core`; line-numbered `Get-Content` for `include/navigation/state_defs.h`, `include/navigation/filter_contracts.h`, `src/navigation/filter_contracts.cpp`, `src/navigation/filter_reset.cpp`, `src/navigation/process_model_inekf.cpp`, `src/navigation/measurement_model_common.cpp`, `src/navigation/measurement_model_gnss.cpp`, `src/navigation/measurement_model_road.cpp`, `src/navigation/measurement_model_uwb.cpp`, `src/navigation/filter_engine.cpp`
- artifacts: `walkthrough.md`
- metrics: code audit only, no new runtime artifacts. Core positive evidence: `BuildInEkfSemantics()` selects `AttitudeErrorConvention::kInvariantBodyError`; `InjectErrorState()` interprets `dx(pos/vel/att)` as `rho_p_body/rho_v_body/phi_body`, maps them through `C_bn/R_ne`, and right-multiplies attitude with `QuatMultiply(state_.q, dq)`; `BuildInEkfResetGamma()` applies the coupled `pos/vel/att` reset with `-Skew(rho_p_body)` and `-Skew(rho_v_body)` blocks; `BuildInEkfProcessLinearization()` uses body-rate/body-force terms (`omega_ib_b_corr`, `f_b_corr`) for the core `0-8` block; `BuildGnssPositionMeasurement()` switches to a body-frame residual with `H_pos=I`, `H_att=-Skew(d_body)`, `H_gnss_lever=I`. Main caveats: `State`/`StateIdx` still expose a 31D vector-state layout (`p/v/phi`) rather than an explicit group object; `BuildZuptMeasurement()` remains additive-velocity form; `BuildUwbMeasurement()` remains pure ECEF additive range form; `InjectErrorState()` still contains one dead `else if (use_inekf)` compatibility branch that no longer executes.
- artifact_mtime: `walkthrough.md @ 2026-04-07 current-session update`
- config_hash_or_mtime: no runtime config or production code changed in this audit-only session; the conclusion is grounded in direct inspection of the current source tree.
- dataset_time_window: no dataset replay executed in this session.
- result_freshness_check: this is a source audit, not a replay. Accepted evidence comes from the live code presently in the workspace rather than any stale historical summary.
- observability_notes: no new schedule or ablation run occurred. The audit conclusion is strongest for the core INS blocks `0-8` plus GNSS lever block `28-30` in the pure `INS/GNSS` path. The ODO-related extrinsic/constraint blocks `21-27` and non-GNSS measurements are not yet all expressed in the same clean invariant style, so the broader 31-state integrated system should still be described as “core InEKF path implemented, but not every measurement chain fully group-native”.
- decision: for the current pure `INS/GNSS` experiment path, the implementation does satisfy the core InEKF idea you described: `P/V/A` correction coordinates are treated as body-frame invariant error coordinates and injected multiplicatively rather than as the old additive navigation-frame error. However, I would not yet describe the whole codebase as a fully explicit, end-to-end Lie-group InEKF implementation for every enabled sensor chain, because some measurement models still use additive wrappers and one dead compatibility branch remains in the reset/injection code.
- next_step: if we want the implementation to be unquestionably “full InEKF” in code-review terms, the next cleanup should remove the dead injection branch and audit/convert `ZUPT/UWB` (and any remaining non-GNSS measurements) so their residuals and Jacobians are expressed directly in the same invariant body-frame contract instead of relying on additive-form reuse or leaving additive models in place.

The new diagnostic conclusion is about the reset Jacobian, not user-facing observability improvement: the reset stayed materially non-identity across live corrections, but outage-position accuracy still remained effectively neutral relative to the canonical `ESKF` reference.
- decision: unified `InEKF` is definitely active on the current runtime path. The near-overlap with `ESKF` in this pure `INS/GNSS` outage experiment is not because the solver silently fell back to standard reset or because `Gamma` stayed numerically equal to `I`; instead, the live reset Jacobian is usually non-identity, while the resulting user-facing trajectory difference remains small under this contract.
- next_step: return to `HYP-15` and trace representative sparse-10s GNSS updates through `measurement_model_gnss.cpp -> filter_engine.cpp -> filter_reset.cpp`, explicitly breaking out `rho_p_body/rho_v_body/phi_body` and `Gamma`, then decide whether the few large `gamma_diff > 1` spikes justify a dedicated targeted study or whether a pure `INS/GNSS` InEKF noise sweep should remain deferred.

Extending the off-window length degrades user-facing position observability strongly for both filters, but the degradation is essentially symmetric under this contract, so the longer outage alone still does not create a material `ESKF/InEKF` separation.
- decision: extending GNSS-off from `100 s` to `150 s` is enough to make the outage problem much harder, but not enough by itself to produce a large `ESKF/InEKF` gap. The current longer-outage evidence therefore supports escalating the perturbation type, not just the outage length, if we want to expose a stronger behavioral difference.
- next_step: keep the `60/150` pair as the next-harder outage reference, then combine it with a stronger perturbation source such as manual-init offsets or lever/prior uncertainty before judging whether the pure `INS/GNSS` outage contract can separate `ESKF` and `InEKF` materially.

- metrics: fresh pytest gate returned `2 passed in 0.76s`. Stable-yaw settle times stayed almost identical across filters: `+10 deg` gives `5/2/1 deg = 10.995/12.995/13.995 s` for both; `+20 deg` gives `ESKF 12.995/13.995/14.995 s` vs `InEKF 11.995/13.995/14.995 s`; `+30 deg` gives `ESKF 12.995/14.995/15.995 s` vs `InEKF 12.995/13.995/15.995 s`. Aggregate robustness separates more as the perturbation grows: `overall_rmse3d ESKF/InEKF = 2.288307/2.292278 m` at `+10 deg`, `2.349440/2.291232 m` at `+20 deg`, and `2.614423/2.294874 m` at `+30 deg`; corresponding `InEKF-ESKF` deltas are `+0.003971 m`, `-0.058207 m`, and `-0.319549 m`. Final 3D errors remain mm-level close in all six runs (`0.003282-0.003364 m`).
- artifact_mtime: `summary.md @ 2026-04-07 23:39:18 local`; `case_metrics.csv @ 2026-04-07 23:39:17 local`; `offset_comparison.csv @ 2026-04-07 23:39:17 local`; representative per-case `all_states` / solver outputs were generated between `23:33` and `23:39 local`
- config_hash_or_mtime: accepted evidence comes from the unchanged `60/150` base config `config_data2_baseline_ins_gnss_eskf_outage_60on150off_best.yaml @ 2026-04-07 23:13:59 local` plus the fresh compare runner/test introduced in-session; solver binary remained `build/Release/eskf_fusion.exe @ 2026-04-07 22:31:39 local`
- dataset_time_window: `data2`, effective truth-aligned run window `t=[528076.009368, 530488.900000]`; phase1=`[528076.0, 528276.0]`; phase2=`[528276.0, 528776.0]`; phase3=`[528776.0, 530488.9]`; schedule remained `60 s on / 150 s off` throughout the compare matrix
- result_freshness_check: all six perturbed-init cases were generated in-session under `output/data2_ins_gnss_outage_60on150off_yaw_init_compare_r1/`; accepted evidence comes from those fresh artifacts and not from any historical summary
- observability_notes: the sensor contract stayed pure `INS/GNSS`; `ODO/NHC/UWB` remained disabled; extrinsic/scale blocks `21-30` stayed frozen / truth-fixed exactly as in the longer-outage reference. The only changed knob was the manual PVA start attitude, and specifically yaw. Under this schedule the initial yaw transient converges quickly for both filters during early GNSS availability, but the larger-offset runs show that downstream position observability under later GNSS outages degrades more severely for `ESKF` than for `InEKF`.
- decision: the stronger nonlinearity probe succeeded partially. It did not uncover a large yaw-convergence-speed gap, but it did show that large yaw-init errors make `InEKF` more robust in aggregate outage accuracy, especially at `+30 deg`, where `overall_rmse3d` improves by about `0.32 m` relative to `ESKF`.
- next_step: if the research target is specifically “who converges faster,” tighten the transient readout further with earlier or stricter thresholds (for example `0.5 deg`, `0.2 deg`, or short-horizon yaw integral error). If the target is “who is more robust under nonlinear starts + outages,” this experiment already supports moving on to phase-wise error decomposition for the `+20/+30 deg` cases rather than increasing yaw offset further.

- observability_notes: this session directly tested observability of blocks `21-27` by freezing one suspect block at a time. With `odo_lever` truth-fixed from phase1, block `25-27` is removed from estimation while `mounting` and `odo_scale` remain active; navigation improves only modestly and `mounting` stays partially observable, so `odo_lever` is a contributor but not the sole source of the remaining error. With `mounting` truth-fixed from phase1, block `22-24` is removed from estimation while `odo_lever` remains active; `odo_lever` does not improve materially, and phase3 navigation degrades sharply despite perfect mounting, which indicates the current bottleneck is not “mounting error alone” and likely still involves coupled excitation/conditioning with persistent `bg_z`.
- decision: keep both truth-fix controls as fresh anchors. The `odo_lever` truth-fix run is directionally helpful but only modestly so; the `mounting` truth-fix run is actively harmful to overall navigation while leaving `odo_lever` almost unchanged. The next sweep should therefore not prioritize mounting-only truth-fix as the mainline remedy.
- next_step: compare the baseline and `fix_odo_lever_truth_fullrun` runs in more detail, then design a follow-up sweep around `bg_z` conditioning and phase2 excitation/P0/Q for blocks `21-27`; only revisit mounting truth-fix if we specifically want to explain the new phase3 degradation mechanism.

- next_step: move the next experiment away from simple `bg_z` noise retuning and toward structural interventions: phase2 excitation/window-length changes, an explicit `bg_z` observability-gate style mechanism, or more targeted block constraints that can change the coupling itself rather than just its noise magnitudes.
